# IAHWG Session Transcripts

Complete transcripts from 7 Informal Ad Hoc Working Group sessions (Sep-Nov 2025).

## Session 1: Initial Discussion on Mandate Creation (Sep 16, 2025)
Video: /video/k1k/k1k41vpaer

**IAHWG**, Co-Chair
Colleagues, if you could please be seated so that we can begin. Thank you. I call to order the first meeting of the Informal Ad Hoc Working Group. On behalf of the co chairs, I extend a warm welcome to all of you to this first meeting of the Informal Ad Hoc Working Group. I would like to recognize the presence of the President of the General Assembly, Her Excellency Annalina Baerbock and Mr. Guy Ryder, under Secretary General Policy in the Executive Office of the Secretary General.

**IAHWG** | Brian Wallace, Co-Chair
Madam President, in our role as Co Chairs of the Informal Ad Hoc Working Group, we congratulate you on your election and wish you a fruitful 80th session of the General Assembly. As members are aware in its decision 79571 of 2 September 2025, the General assembly decided to establish an Informal Ad Hoc Working Group open to all Member States and observers to consider options to improve the creation, delivery and review of UN mandates. The establishment of this group is a milestone within the broader UN80 initiative, and new Zealand and Jamaica are honored to co chair its work. Today we gather with a clear sense of purpose to take forward the mandate entrusted to us by the Assembly. In the spirit of cooperation, openness and trust that defines multilateralism at its best, our leaders have called for a United nations that is more effective, more efficient and fit for purpose. As it marks its 80th anniversary, this working Group is one expression of that collective ambition, and it is for us, the membership, to shape how that conviction is translated into practice. We meet today to set out our understanding of the task before us and to engage with you on how we can best work together to complete it successfully. While we have some initial thoughts on how we might proceed, today is not about prescribing a roadmap. It is about listening, taking stock of your perspectives, and beginning to build a common understanding of the way forward. Mandates derive from the will of Member States, and it is vital that all delegations have the opportunity to contribute. We are therefore committed to proceeding in a manner that is fully open, transparent and inclusive, ensuring that the Working Group reflects the the broadest possible participation and ownership. At the same time, we are mindful of the Assembly's clear instruction that we must strive for consensus as we begin to prepare a program of work and plan our way forward. We are eager to hear from you so that we can be sure that our proposed approach aligns with the needs and wishes of the membership. We also recognize the many demands on delegations, particularly smaller missions, in the months ahead. And for this reason we see value in beginning with a Discovery Phase A period of wide consultations to gather perspectives, to clarify priorities and to build shared understandings. This will allow us to develop a package of principles and follow up actions that could form the basis an agreed outcome. This phase will be fully open and inclusive and organized in a way that is sensitive to the competing demands on delegation's time. We will also draw on the best data analysis and expertise available, including through active support from the Secretariat. And we thank the Under Secretary General for his firm commitment in this regard. It is also clear to us that there are many outside the Working Group who wish to contribute ideas for our collective consideration. We welcome this and will facilitate it as part of the Working Group process while preserving the Member State driven nature of our discussions. We will aim to complete this phase in time to report back to the membership by the 15th of December in line with the Assembly's request, before moving into a production phase to finalize outcomes by March 2026. With that, I now pass the floor to Ambassador Schwargov for some additional comments.

**IAHWG** | Carolyn Schwalger, Co-Chair
Thank you Ambassador Wallace and good morning everybody. President of the General Assembly Under Secretary General Guy Ryder and all of our colleagues. It's so great to see so many of you here this morning. The General assembly has given us clear direction. We are tasked with identifying principles and follow up actions to improve the creation, delivery and review of mandates. The Secretary General's report on the Mandate Implementation Review provides a useful starting point for these discussions. It provides a number of proposed solutions and follow up actions for for implementation by the UN Secretariat in support of Member States. We will invite the UN Secretariat to provide the Working Group with updates on implementation of those proposals that sit within their authority at appropriate moments during this process. The report also proposes a range of actions that Member States could take to enhance mandate design, improve mandate delivery and support mandate Review as you engage in the Working Group, we would welcome your feedback on these proposals, focusing on those actions which you consider most important to progress and or those where Member States could achieve some quick wins. We also understand that Working Group members will also have ideas of their own on concrete actions we can take beyond those proposed in the Report. We encourage you to bring these to the consideration of this Working Group. Let us also assure you that we have learned many lessons from the last mandate review almost 20 years ago. One of the key findings of that process was the impossibility of trying to have a Working Group such as this make judgments on individual mandates. As Co Chairs, we intend to focus our attention at the system level. We will not be considering individual mandates in this Working Group. Further, as Co Chairs, we think it will be important to focus on the future so that we can be more effective and efficient with with limited resources. We want to hear from you what that future might look like. How can Member States, who are responsible for the adoption of mandates, be more effective and more efficient in future? What principles should underpin how we work together as Member States to strengthen the impact of the United nations, to improve delivery across all pillars of of our work? And what principles should underpin our partnership with the Secretariat going forward? As Co Chairs, we do not intend to prejudge what the outputs of the Working Group should be or what form these might take, although we can imagine a scenario where they might involve a combination of different elements. This is for the Working Group members to determine together. We want to hear from you today and in the coming weeks about your desired level of ambition and what good might look like in terms of our outputs. We hope to forge consensus amongst Working Group members on some principles to underpin how we collectively keep better sight of the overall mandate landscape, how we deal with duplication and overlap between mandates and what we do with mandates which might have outlived their original purpose. We will be asking you how we can mitigate the unreasonable burden these aggregated instructions place on us as Member States and on the UN system, as well as what principles might underpin the creation of mandates that translate into clearer, fairer and more sustainable resource allocations. We will also need to consider how any principles and actions we agree should be applied in practice, including in relation to mandates originating in UN bodies outside of New York. With that, I would now like to pass the floor to my Co Chair, Ambassador Wallace, to outline our thinking on the relationship between the Mandate process and the wider UN80 initiative process process.

**IAHWG** | Brian Wallace, Co-Chair
Ambassador, thank you so much. Co Chair. We acknowledge that this process will unfold in parallel with the other UN 80 work streams on operational efficiencies and structural and programmatic changes. We will therefore remain attentive to developments across the Initiative, while keeping our focus firmly on the mandate provided to this Group Group by the General Assembly. Across all of our endeavors, we will be guided by the shared aspiration of the membership for a more effective and efficient United Nations. The issues before us are significant, representing our collective strategic vision and operational expectations of the UN as a whole. This is why at this stage, engagement at the level of permanent representatives is especially important. The political vision and strategic direction you bring will provide the compass by which this process is steered. With the expertise of colleagues to follow in due course as our work becomes more technical, colleagues as co chairs, we know the discussions ahead of us will be demanding and complex. However, it is with optimism and conviction that we believe this Working Group provides an excellent opportunity to improve how the United nations delivers for the communities we serve. The strength of this Working Group will not lie in a document or a deadline, but in the quality of dialogue we foster together. If we succeed in creating a space that is constructive, candid and forward looking, we will have laid the foundation not only for this process, but for a stronger multilateral system. Let us therefore seize this moment with a sense of common purpose and shared responsibility. The United nations belongs to all of us and together we can ensure that it is equipped to meet the demands of today and the aspirations of tomorrow. We thank you for the trust you have placed in us. I now give the floor to the President of the General Assembly, Her Excellency Annalina Baerbock.

**GA** | Annalena Baerbock, PGA
Thank you, Excellencies, ladies and gentlemen, I'm pleased to join this inaugural meeting of the informal Ad hoc Working Group on the Mandate Implementation review under the UNAT initiative. And I thank His Excellency, Mr. Brian Wallace, Permanent Representative of Jamaica, and Her Excellency, Ms. Carlene Schwalger, Permanent Representative of New Zealand, for their leadership and for bringing us together today. I would like to also thank the Co Chairs of the revitalization process from Romania and South Africa. We have worked also closely together and this is an outcome of your excellent work. So thank you very much. And I think the presence today underlines the importance of this Working group because we are living, as we have heard, in challenging times and therefore also all of us as General assembly, do have a special responsibility in this process to take forward the Secretary General's report on mandate implementation, to distill guiding principles and to chart the next step that will make our mandates clearer, more effective and more accountable. Underlining that it's not only paper, but that it's really implementation which matters. It builds on the dialogues begun last session by my predecessor, President Philemon Yang, and takes us to the next steps in this process. And I'm also thankful to him and his team team for keeping me fully informed during the transition period. And I intend to build upon their efforts and their open door. I would like to also underline that this process of us as the General assembly is obviously part of the heart of the UNAD process on the adapting this organization for the 21st century. Ensuring that our institution, that we are really fit for the future, that we really deliver as an institution on the efficiency level but also on the state of art level, like other institutions around the world. And therefore, I would like to recall the three themes of the UN80 process. Guy Raider will definitely go deeper into it, but I think it's good, good to have it always in mind when we speak about the mandates. First, to sharpen the efficiency, which includes cutting bureaucracy, reducing cost. We have learned altogether what every minute costs here and making smarter use of our global presence. Second is the mandate review itself, ensuring the many tasks entrusted to the UN remain focused and relevant. And third, consider the system as a whole, drawing on the first two streams to assess whether deeper structural or programmatic changes are needed. So colleagues, in my opening address I spoke explicitly about this make it or break it moment, that this mandate review process is part of it, whether we make it or we break it. And therefore, I believe and would like to underline what the co chairs have said, that we should take up this topic with a positive spirit, that we together can actually make it. And that UN80 is not just an exercise in reform for reform itself. Definitely not a cut cutting exercise for just cutting cost, but it's a chance for us to make this institution better and stronger together. It is a chance to prove that the UN can deliver more effectively and accountably for the people and it serves. And the mandate review is an essential component of this because this is about us. This is where we as Member States, you and we as a GA in general can show that we are delivering, that we are leading by good examples ourselves. Less than two weeks in office and already five mandate events plus two additional high level events are on the agenda next week. So I for myself tasked myself to always think with every new mandate and every session I chair, what could I learn for the future, to make it in the future more effective and more accountable to the people. Because I believe that the organization cannot continue to layer more mandates on top of old ones, but has to focus on delivery efficiency and effectiveness. And therefore I would like to give you a very small example. When we were preparing for now the upcoming high Level Speak week, like the ceremonial event on Monday, the Beijing platform based on resolutions and people told me, especially the Secretariat, every minute counts, it costs thousands of euro, but. But then I have a resolution saying you should put 16 speakers in one hour. So this doesn't work at all. But I cannot do anything about it because it's in there in the resolution. So I think looking really at this tiny examples where we can save a lot of money but also reflect all the time, not we've done it always like it always the speaker from there and there and there and there. But just reflect how we can learn also from the past. So definitely this is not an easy undertaking because everybody loves their darlings and this is I think also something which we could reflect to look really when we are presenting things, how we can lead by good examples. Again, I'd like to underline what the co chairs have said. Obviously it's not about now and the past, but looking for the future which also gives us strength that we can deliver on this very challenging timetable. In this regard I applaud you of the timetable. Yes, it's ambitious. I've heard already that some people say it might be a bit too ambitious, but I would say if it would be easy then others could do the job. So we work on that one together so that we can deliver as best as we can. My office, the OPGA will support wherever support is needed. Also on transparency because obviously trust is the base for the work here together. So on this note I'm pleased that we were able to provide last minute also the public support for this discussion today and we are keen of keeping this transparency and the support also in the future. So thank you very much for the exchange today and I'm really looking forward of working together. On that one last mentioning, I would like to say I think it's of highest importance that this does not only stay in the room, but this is really taking up to senior level engagements. So with the high level week ahead, please prepare every head of State and minister visiting the PGA that I will double check if they have heard about UNAT before and the mandate review because obviously it is also an opportunity where we can show all together that we are not only working here together in New York, but also in the capitals in this regard. Looking forward to a great hey, Labor Week and also to a great working group. Thank you.

**IAHWG**, Co-Chair
I thank the President. We have also requested Mr. Guy Ryder, under Secretary General for Policy in the Executive Office of the Secretary General to deliver some remarks on the support he and his team will be providing to this process. I now give the floor to the Under Secretary General.

**UN Secretariat** | Guy Ryder, USG Policy
Thank you very much, President of the 80th session of the General Assembly. Co Chairs of this informal ad hoc working group. Let me begin by congratulating the co chairs, Ambassador Wallace and Ambassador S.H. schwalger for their appointment to co chair this informal ad hoc working group on the UN80 initiative. Ladies and gentlemen, the Secretary General has welcomed the adoption of resolution 79318 which endorsed the overall direction of the UN 80 initiative and we have taken note of the General Assembly's encouragement to submit proposals to strengthen the impact and the agility of the United nations while reducing duplication and improving mandate delivery. And as the President of the General assembly has indicated, the 80th anniversary is an important opportunity to build on and to intensify the reforms of past years. The UN80 initiative aims to move us towards an effective and sustainable United nations and Decision 79571 established the Informal Ad Hoc Working Group and the decision establishes that the Working Group will consider in its scope the proposals contained in the Secretary General's report on the Mandate implementation review and identify principles and follow up actions in order to improve the creation, delivery and review of mandates. The timeline set out in that decision is certainly ambitious and I want to recognise your efforts in organising Co chairs this first meeting exactly two weeks after the adoption of the decision and your appointment and let me just take a moment today to speak to the proposals contained in the report by the Secretary General as a, I hope, important input to the work of this Working Group and we would gladly provide a technical briefing on specific aspects of the report if you request it. Let me speak first to the areas outlined in the report in which the Secretary General will act to improve support to Member States throughout the mandate life cycle and these are listed in the report on the Mandate Implementation Review. To enhance mandate visibility and design, the UN system would accelerate the creation of mandate registries, improve Secretariat support, develop new tools and complement existing statements of expenditures with additional information on related programmatic activities. To improve reporting, the UN system will provide shorter reports, combine reports, introduce different report formats and publish download statistics and to improve mandate delivery management, the UN system will strengthen internal oversight, review mandate citations, better use system wide coordination platform reforms and apply all UN system commitments in the Funding Compact and to establish effective review mechanisms, the UN system will increase use of existing mechanisms to identify opportunities to consolidate and to streamline work and to strengthen results based management. The United Nations Systems is working on a roadmap on how these different actions can be taken by the UN system in each of these areas and we will be able to provide you with further information on this internal roadmap if the Working Group requires it at a future meeting. If you request it, let me turn to the proposals now submitted by the Secretary General in his report on the Mandate Implementation Review that Member States may wish to consider as part of this intergovernmental process. To enhance mandate design, Member States may wish to reduce the length of mandate texts, frame mandates to allow the Secretary General appropriate flexibility and refrain from mandating new tasks without corresponding resources. To improve mandate delivery, Member States may wish to prioritise requests in mandates, fully apply all commitments by Member States through the Funding Compact and allow UN system entities greater flexibility to redeploy resources quickly and to support mandate review. Member States may wish to systematise and to reinforce mandate review mechanisms, include expiry clauses and resolutions, introduce collective reviews of mandates and streamline how mandates are discussed. Co Chairs, Distinguished delegates, in decision 79, 571, you have requested the Secretary General to provide substantive support to the Working Group as needed for the effective discharge of its mandate. As you determine how you wish to organise the work of this Working Group, the UN system is at your disposal. At the report's launch, many of you indicated that you would welcome further information on the data analysis and proposals across the mandate life cycle, and the Secretariat stands ready to provide an informal briefing on the data and insights in the report. As we recognise in the report, ultimately, Member States are own the mandates that they give to the UN system and that Member States also decide on next steps. We are here to be of assistance. In your letter inviting me to this meeting, Co Chairs, you suggested that I speak to the support the UN system can provide to the Working Group's work, such as through the provision of additional data and analysis on each of the areas from the report that I have referred to in my remarks today, the UN system stands ready to provide you with that further information as you request it. For example, with regard to what is already in the report, I indicated earlier that you could request us to provide information on internal actions that we are taking, and we can also provide further background on the proposals that the Secretary General suggested Member States might wish to consider themselves or on the date that underpins the report. That said, as I have already indicated, it is for you to determine how you wish to organise this work and we remain at the full disposal of the Working Group. I thank you.

**IAHWG**, Co-Chair
I thank the Under Secretary General. I now open the floor for statements by delegations. Please press the microphone button if you wish to speak. Please approach the Secretariat if you are speaking on behalf of a group of States. Participants are reminded that statements are limited to five minutes for statements on behalf of groups and three minutes for statements in your national capacity. Participants are also reminded to send their statement via the E Submit module on the Edelegate Platform. Platform it's now my honour to give the floor to the Permanent Representative of Iraq, Speaking for the G77, the floor is yours.

**IRQ**, Permanent Representative
President of General Assembly Under Secretary General Excellencies Co Chairs I have the honor to deliver this statement on behalf of the group of 77 and China. @ the onset, allow me to congratulate both of you. Her Excellency Caroline Schwalga and Permanent Representative of New Zealand and His Excellency Mr. Brian Wallace, permanent Representative of Jamaica, on your appointment as Co Chairs of the Informal Ad Hoc Working Group on the Mandate Implementation Review and the Work Stream 2 of the UN 80 initiative. The group looks forward to working closely with you and we welcome that Our first meeting is dedicated to setting the tone of of the process. The group views the UN8 initiative as an important step towards strengthening the role of the United nations in addressing global challenges. We stress that any proposal under this Initiative and its three work streams must fully respect the purposes and principles of the Charter of the United nations as well as the intergovernmental nature of the organization. The UN 80 process should reinforce, not dilute, multilateralism, ensure equitable participation of all Member States and address the priorities and concerns of developing countries. The Group reaffirms the importance of learning from the past experiences to avoid repeating previous mistakes. The earlier exercise, conducted about two decades ago, required significant effort but yielded limited results. In this regard, the Group request a detailed briefing by the Secretary on that process, which extended over several years. It would further assist in ensuring that the informal Ad hoc Working Group fully benefits the from prior lessons learned. It's therefore crucial to build on the outcomes of every review process undertaken so far in order to prevent duplications of effort in a process that is itself aimed at avoiding redundancy. We must build upon what has already been agreed on to ensure our collective effort are not wasted. The Group underlines three guiding principles. First, the spirit of consensus. Second, Member State driven decision making and third, maintaining balance among the three pillars of the United nations. With development as a parity. The Group underscores the importance of ensuring that the establishment and work plan of the Ad Hoc Working Group are conducted in a manner that allows for meaningful and inclusive deliberations. We therefore support adopting a flexible timeline for its meetings, taking into account the concern of Member States, particularly given that the main segment of the General assembly is already a period of intense engagement across the Preliminary and its six main Committees. Such flexibility would help create a more conducive environment for constructive discussions and allow all delegations to participate effectively, including smaller ones. Further, the Group underscored the importance of ensuring that negotiations and decision making processes are conducted in an open, transparent and inclusive manner through established intergovernmental arrangements, norms and procedures. We trust that the future consideration of such important matters will be pursued on the basis of broad consultations, consensus and shared ownership among all Member States. The group of 77 in China will also submit written responses to the Co Chair's guiding questions, underscoring our readiness to engage substantively in the next stages of the process. To conclude, the group of 77 in China stresses that this first meeting is an important opportunity to set a constructive tone and to help shape a positive spirit for this process. The Group reiterates its commitment to engage constructively and to ensure that this process remains inclusive, transparent and efficient with the full participation of all Member States. I thank you.

**IAHWG**, Co-Chair
I thank the Permanent Representative of Iraq and I now give the floor to the Permanent Representative of Singapore, speaking on behalf of a Group of Students States.

**SGP**, Permanent Representative
Thank you very much. Co Chairs, I have the honor to make this statement on behalf of the Small States Group ssg, which is a cross regional grouping of small States comprising developed and developing countries. The list of countries that have aligned with this statement will be circulated after the meeting, but I'm pleased to inform members that this statement is supported by a group of 50 countries and we anticipate that more small States will join future statements within this Working Group. The Small States Group welcomes the establishment of this informal Ad Hoc Working Group on Mandate Implementation Review. We take this opportunity to congratulate the two Co Chairs on the appointment and we have every confidence that both of you will lead the process to a successful outcome for small States. An Effective Multilateralism A multilateral system underpinned by respect for the UN Charter and international law is not an option, but an existential necessity. The 80th anniversary of the founding of the UN is therefore not only a moment for reflection about the future of our multilateral system, it is also an opportunity to reform and re energize the un. It is no secret that the multilateral system is under severe stress as a result of geopolitical tensions, economic fragmentation and unilateralism. The establishment of this Working Group is therefore a timely and essential exercise to reposition the UN and streamline its work to deliver results for all our countries. We wish to make three points. First, the Ad Hoc Working Group is a Member States driven process. It is therefore entirely in our hands to review all aspects of the mandate lifecycle as a means to reimagine and reposition the UN and to avoid duplication, enhance efficiency and deliver results on the ground. There's no doubt that all three streams of the UN 80 initiative are interconnected and the success of this process will have an impact on the other two work streams. With the use of new AI tools, we are better positioned to make sense of the UN mandates landscape in all parts of the UN ecosystem. At this early stage of this process, we believe it is important to keep an open mind, not rule anything out and allow for a discussion of all proposals and perspectives. Secondly, the ad hoc working group should be forward looking and ambitious while avoiding the pitfalls and politicization that plagued previous UN reform efforts. While we should be ambitious, we should avoid an all or nothing approach. It is important that we take an incremental and pragmatic approach that can show results in this regard. Our work in this process must be based on data and analyses on the UN's mandates landscape which will provide evidence based insights on how best to move forward. Ultimately, our objective is to achieve the effective implementation of mandates while avoiding duplication and inefficiencies. In this regard, our process will strengthen the three pillars of the UN system so that it can deliver what has been agreed and adopted. Thirdly, the success of this Working group depends on political will and mutual trust among Member States. In this regard, we as a group of small States are committed to participating constructively to finding solutions and to build consensus. We are encouraged by the fact that all Member States have acknowledged the need for a more efficient and stronger UN system. This gives us hope that we can collectively find solutions for the benefit of all our countries and people quotas. The UN 80 initiative is an opportunity to imagine a better future for the multilateral system. In order for the UN to continue serving its purpose and our peoples, Member States must take responsibility in reshaping the mandate system which lies at the heart of how the UN functions and works. We stand ready to work with the Co Chairs and with all Member States on achieving a meaningful mandate implementation review in line with the objectives of birth. Thank you very much for your attention.

**IAHWG**, Co-Chair
I thank the Permanent Representative of Singapore speaking for the Small States Group. And I now give the floor to the representative of guinea speaking for the African Group. The floor is yours.

**GIN**, Representative
Thank you. Co Chairs, Excellencies, I have the honor to deliver this statement on behalf of the African Group. At the outset, we wish to congratulate Ambassador Caroline Schwalger from New Zealand and Ambassador Brian Wallace from Jamaica on their recent appointment as Co Chairs. We are confident in your leadership and abilities to steer our collective effort with utmost transparency and inclusivity, adhering to establishing the governmental norms and procedures that underpin this process, aligning with the statement from the Permanent Representative of Iraq on behalf of the group of 77 and China, the African Group wishes to make a few additional remarks. We recognize the urgent need to streamline mandates to alleviate unnecessary administrative burdens on the United Nations. The effectiveness of any reforms must enhance the Organization's responsiveness to the diverse priorities and pressing needs of Member States and the population we serve. While we collectively recognize the importance of to enhancing mandate implementation and streamlining outputs, it is imperative that the core mandates across all three pillars of the United nations, particularly the Development Pillar, are preserved. The Working Group should remain open and receptive to a broader array of ideas beyond those outlined in the Secretary General's Report. Moreover, it is crucial to adopt a realistic and focused approach when establishing meaningful and achievable targets. While ambition is important, it must align with existing realities to avoid repeating past failures in achieving intended outcomes. The Working Group should not duplicate the work of existing bodies. Rather, it should leverage those forums to address specific aspects, thereby allowing the Working Group to concentrate on its core objectives. Furthermore, while the Secretariat plays a vital role in advancing efficiencies, intergovernmental organs must safeguard the integrity of mandates as outlined by the UN Secretary General. Reform efforts should should proceed with full authority and oversight from Member States, ensuring transparency and inclusivity. Our discussion must be guided by foundational principles. Establishing realistic and achievable time frames is essential for interactive and constructive dialogues. This will enable meaningful deliberation without the pressure of rushed timelines. It is vital for the Working Group to be cognizant of the fact that many Member States will be actively engaged in the work of various committees and other processes which may hinder their ability to follow multiple discussions simultaneously. A Member State driven approach will enhance the quality of our discussions, fostering creativity and innovation in addressing pressing issues. We must cultivate a culture of consensus in decision making, promoting collaboration and valuing diverse viewpoints. To effectively organize the agenda of the Working Group, we propose a phased instructor approach that allows an in depth examination of key issues. Allocating adequate time for each phase is crucial for meaningful engagement. Additionally, the agenda should reflect the priorities of all Member States while retaining the flexibility to adapt to evolving needs. Implementing regular review points will facilitate the assessment of our progress and recalibrate discussions, ensuring a steadfast commitment to consensus and collaboration. In conclusion, the African Group is committed to actively and constructively participating in the discussions of the informal ad hoc Working Group on the mandate implementation Review. I thank you for your attention.

**IAHWG**, Co-Chair
I thank the representative of guinea speaking for the African Union. And I now give the floor to the representative of the European Union. The floor is yours.

**EU**, Representative
Thank you, Madam Chair, Madam President or the General Assembly. Mr. Undersecretary General Dear Co Chairs, I have the honor to speak on behalf of the European Union and its member states. The candidate countries, Turkey, North Macedonia, Montenegro, Albania, Ukraine, the Republic of Moldova, Bosnia and Herzegovina and Georgia, as well as Armenia, Andorra, Monaco and San Marino, align themselves with this statement at the outset, Allow me to thank the President of the General assembly for her important presence here today and to congratulate the permanent representatives of Jamaica and New Zealand on their appointments as Co Chairs of this informal ad hoc working group. Dear Colleagues, you can count on the EU's full support to your work. The European Union's member states are firmly committed to multilateralism and we are among the UN's leading political supporters and funders. It is precisely because of this commitment that we engage in the UN80 process, recognizing it is a unique opportunity to build a stronger United nations, an organization where its members can make informed decisions, translate these into effective mandates, and ensure the organization efficiently can deliver real impact on the ground for the people it serves, especially for those furthest behind. There is broad recognition that the mandate process has grown unwieldy and that we must look at this with renewed clarity of purpose. We trust that under your guidance, this Working Group can help us review and streamline mandates, improve the creation and delivery, and increase accountability for impact. This will set us on a path that strengthens the UN for the future. In answering the questions that you have posed and following your guidance on how to best structure our discussion, allow me to share the European Union's views as on the question of how to make our discussions interactive, constructive and inclusive, the EU strongly supports a process that is open, transparent and participatory, where every voice can be heard and every delegation has a genuine role to play. We believe that both informal dialogues and more structured meetings, regular opportunities for cross regional exchanges, and the early involvement of the Secretariat's expertise will be essential to keep discussions focused and constructive while ensuring that all perspectives are taken into account. We would also encourage you to reach out to UN global hubs outside of New York to collect the fullest possible perspective on on mandate reform. The Secretary General's and the Secretariat's expertise and analyses will be crucial in helping us make informed choices, improve efficiency and maximize the impact of our collective work. Therefore, we should welcome the Secretariat's readiness to bring its full potential to bear under our guidance so that together we can succeed for the organization as a whole. On the question of the organization of work and sequencing of discussions, we welcome Considering a phased approach, listening widely, consulting deeply and reflecting carefully, including in cross regional settings before moving into more prescriptive text based negotiations will help us all build a better understanding of the work ahead and of different initial ideas and concerns with an open mind and thus help us make more informed and consensual choices. We see merit in organizing the initial period around thematic clusters such as Principles for the Mandate lifecycle, options for improving mandate creation and review, and approaches to implementation so that deliberations can progress in a logical sequence leading into your Progress report by 15 December 2025. On the question of addressing the Secretary General's mandate Implementation Review Report and its recommendations, the EU believes the Working Group should focus on identifying systemic improvements and translating them into practical, results oriented outcomes. At the same time, we should situate our work within the broader context of the UNAD initiative to ensure coherence and to avoid duplication. In our view, a balanced approach drawing on the Secretariat's analytical input, past reform experiences and the priorities outlined in the Pact of the Future will give this group the opportunity to agree on principles as well as specific and concrete actions that can leave a lasting legacy that will guide the organization for years to come. To repeat what we said from the very beginning of this process, in our view at least, the Pact should be our what and the UNAD our how for for guiding the UN's reform and future action. In closing, Co Chairs, the European Union and its Member States stand ready at all levels to support you in this endeavor. We are committed to working with you and with all delegations to turn this process into genuine collective success. Together we can ensure that the UN is more effective and efficient, better equipped for the challenges of today and prepared for the demands of tomorrow. Thank you.

**IAHWG**, Co-Chair
I thank the Permanent Representative of the European Union and I now give the floor to the Permanent Representative of Palau speaking for AOCs.

**PLW**, Permanent Representative
The floor is yours, Madam President. USG Rider distinguished CO Chairs, I have the honor to deliver this statement on behalf of the alliance of Small Island States aoc. We align with the statement delivered by Iraq on behalf of the group of 77 in China and wish to provide the following additional views that are specific to small island developing States at the outset. AUSSIS extends our sincere congratulations to you Co Chairs on your appointment for this important process. We're particularly pleased to see a fellow sids as well as a very good friend of sids leading our Working Group and you can count on our support and cooperation. Distinguished CO Chairs as We mark the 80th anniversary of the United Nations, AOC sees this process as a vital opportunity to reaffirm the UN Charter while modernizing the organization's capacity to deliver for those who need it most, particularly sids. Now allow me to respond to the three guiding questions before us. First, on ensuring that our discussions are interactive, constructive, and inclusive. As many of our members are represented by small delegations, convening meetings of the Working Group in parallel with those of the General Assembly's main Committees during the main session will inevitably prevent us from engaging meaningfully in the process. Therefore, in order to ensure maximum participation by all delegations, efforts should be made to avoid scheduling meetings of the Working Group at the same time as the plenary meetings of the main Committees. We also urge the CO Chairs to ensure early and transparent scheduling and circulation of background materials and to consider organizing most of the substantive work after the conclusion of the main session to ensure that we can all contribute fully to this important work. Second, on organizing and sequencing our discussions While AOC prefers to begin the more substantive aspects of our work after the main session, we also recognize the CO Chair's mandate. In the interim. We believe that the Working Group could focus its effort on more thematic decision discussions guided by the three core areas of the Secretary General's Mandate Implementation Review Report. These sessions would allow Member States to better understand the proposals under consideration, identify key questions, seek clarification and additional data from the report's authors where needed, and provide targeted inputs that can shape the direction of the review. The goal during this initial phase should be to create a common understanding of the issues, identify areas of convergence, and lay the foundation for our more substant extent of work in 2026. Third, on addressing the Secretary General's recommendations in the broader context of the UN80 initiative. As indicated in our earlier statements, AUSIS welcomes the Secretary General's commitment to improving the effectiveness and efficiency of the UN system. The acknowledgement in his Mandate Implementation Review Report of systemic challenges such as fragmented implementation and uneven capacities are acutely felt by sids. At the same time, reform should also preserve investments in programs that serve the most vulnerable. Investment and development mandates, including those supporting the implementation of the Antigua and Barbuda agenda for sids should not be deprioritized under the guise of restructuring. As such, AOC stresses that the Working Group's focus to consider proposals to review or realign mandates should aim to enhance the UN's ability to deliver on the mandates themselves and not result in reducing support for developing countries, particularly sids. Ultimately, realignment must translate into improved mandate delivery for the people and countries who rely on the un. The most distinguished Co Chairs. In closing, AUSS stands ready to engage constructively with you and Member States through the group of 77 to ensure transparent, inclusive and Member States journey and process that strengthens the UN's delivery for all. I thank you.

**AUS**, Permanent Representative
Thank you very much indeed Chair and congratulations to both Co Chairs on their appointment. This has been very significant as an exercise. Thank you President of the General assembly for joining us this morning and also to USG Guy Ryder. I have the honour to speak, as you mentioned, on behalf of Canada, New Zealand and my own delegation Australia. We welcome the establishment of this informal ad hoc working group to develop principles and actions to improve the creation, delivery and review of mandates. Today represents an important step in taking forward the UN 80 initiative process, and we're delighted to be in such capable hands and have great confidence in your leadership. Our delegations acknowledge that the United nations is under pressure, demands for delivery are high and the financial situation is exceptionally challenging. We're committed to working collaboratively in the Fifth Committee to support the adoption of the revised regular budget for this session. We're also waiting with anticipation to see the Secretary General's proposals on structured reforms and program realignment in the near future. While this Working Group is primarily focused on mandates, Cairns acknowledges the interconnected nature of the three UN 80 initiative work streams. This Working Group will need to be mindful of the other UN80 work streams as it carries out its work if we're to achieve a UN system that that is more effective and responsive now and into the future. We welcome the CO Chair's proposed approach as outlined this morning. A process which is inclusive, transparent, data driven, creative, open minded, and which reflects the varied priorities of Member States and observers will be essential. This Working Group provides an opportunity to take a more strategic approach to how mandates are created, funded, implemented and reviewed. As noted on 1 August, Cairns welcomes the proposals in the Secretary General's Mandate Implementation Review Report as important substantive input to the work of the Working Group. As we touched on the 2nd of September, we also believe the following points will be key to achieving meaningful and lasting reform through this Working Group. First, we consider how to improve mandates at the system level. We we need to learn the lessons from almost 20 years ago when a similar mandate exercise was conducted as were ultimately unsuccessful because it focused on reviewing individual mandates. The sheer number of existing mandates means a mandate by mandate approach in this Working Group is simply not feasible in the time that we have available. Second, the development and sharing of comprehensive information and analysis by the Secretariat, including but not limited to the online registry of mandates, will be crucial to help members of the Working Group understand how we might do better in drafting, implementing and evaluating mandates. Third, we encourage this Working Group to focus on how we might collectively develop practical measures to reduce duplication, eliminate redundancies, link mandate decisions with projected costs, enhance efficiencies in implementation and and terminate mandates that we agree have become obsolete. The upcoming Committee season is an opportunity to reflect on those issues and consider matters we could take forward in this Working Group. Fourth, we note that some of the recommendations in the report are within the existing authorities and remit of the Secretary General. We encourage the Secretary General to make full use of his authorities to action these recommendations as soon as possible and for this Working Group to focus on those issues that require approval or action by Member States. Finally, we echo the call for strengthened monitoring and assessment of mandate implementation. This is essential to ensure our commitments here in New York and other United nations fora translate into impact on the ground. CAANS looks forward to working constructively with our fellow Working Group members on practical steps to strengthen the the capacity of the United nations to deliver its mandates. Thank you very much.

**CHE**, Representative
Thank you Co Chair and I would like to start by joining colleagues and extending our warmest congratulations on your appointment as Co Chairs. This review therefore must strengthen all these pillars in a balanced manner and avoid treating them in isolation. The review must also be the subject to constructive engagement by all Member States, each of which must be prepared to make concessions so that the UN's work is sustainable, effective and in line with available resources. So our approach will be based on four principles. First, combating duplication of must be a priority. Mandates are an essential framework for UN action, but when they overlap they fragment the system and instead they should reinforce existing areas of expertise, for example in the fields of health, humanitarian action or human rights, where knowledge and capacity are already concentrated. To this end, intra and institutional competition must be avoided and the core capacities of entities must be be adequately funded. Second, build on what works the Quadrennial Comprehensive Policy Review. The QCPR illustrates how Member States can provide policy guidance without reopening individual mandates. The resulting reform of the United nations development System proves that clear guidance can realign the system and produce results. Similarly, functional support services should be consolidated, shared and strengthened by not dismantled. The measures envisaged must aim for long term efficiency and be based on sound cost benefit analysis. Third, mandates must be forward looking. They must be clear, coherent and adequately resourced to be credible and effective, but they must also anticipate tomorrow's challenges and benefit from technological advances and the interaction between science and diplomacy. Fourth, the responsibility of Member States Ultimately, it is up to us to ensure the coherence of the system in the General assembly as well as in the governing bodies of the specialized agencies. While fully respecting their autonomy, we must act coherently in all the bodies in which we participate. This also means that the review must go beyond the Secretariat alone and cover the entire United nations system. We have a unique opportunity to rethink and strengthen the system. Switzerland is ready to work constructively with all delegations to ensure that this review brings about concrete improvements. Switzerland is determined to continue to offer the full support of Geneva, a place of inclusiveness, innovation, digital development and scientific foresight that will increase the effectiveness of the United nations as a whole. **ARG**, Representative
Good morning, colleagues, Distinguished Co Chairs, PGA Under Secretary Ryder in addition to the statement delivered by the Xi77 and China, the Argentine delegation expresses the following on its national capacity, the UN 80 initiative represents an opportunity to evaluate the overall functioning of the organization and seek convergences to promote more efficient and effective functioning of the United nations system while optimizing the fulfillment of the mandates. Eight years after its creation, we must remember that the organization was established with the objective of preserving international peace and security, resolving disputes among its members and defending the freedom and rights of individuals. Therefore, we must focus in the principles of the Charter and thus reassess the role of the institution recognized by society as a forum for the peaceful resolution between states. We must also make accurate and realistic diagnosis and recognized that in recent years certain agendas had been oversized, generating inefficiencies and distancing the work of the UN from its original mandates. Peace, security and development. We recognize the role of the Member States, based on their sovereign powers, in providing political guidelines to the UN system among and supervising its work, and the role of the Secretary General as a Chief Administrative officer in promoting the necessary administrative reforms. The UN 80 also represents an opportunity to have a more efficient UN system and the management of administrative and financial resources, reducing expenses and eliminating overlapping functions. In this exercise, we must assume shared responsibility between Member States and the UN system for the proliferation of certain mandates, but also for the proliferation of parallel initiatives, meetings and agendas that, without an intergovernmental mandate, lead to an oversizing and duplication of certain agendas and debates. Co Chairs we must take into account existing debates and formal spaces. For example, the recent process of revitalizing the working methods of the General Assembly. The UN 80 initiative is structural and comprehensive and we therefore await the result of the 2026 budget review and the World Stream 3 report. The review of mandates is a very important and sensitive issue and therefore must be addressed prudently and specifically without resorting the general approaches of principles. Under the one size fits all concept. Regarding the work of this other group, we consider it necessary to to have a predictable roadmap for the coming months, avoiding overlaps with the key moment of the Committee's work, especially for small and medium sized delegation and generate, as you said, quality dial IO. Additionally, and as a preliminary idea, we wish to preserve the General Rule that General assembly resolutions remain valid until they are fully implemented and not be undermined by sunset clause. Finally, the Group the Working Group could follow the methodology of the Secretary General's report organized into three stages, mandate creation, mandate execution and mandate review. The Group could focus its work on the first two stages and in this initial phase, considering the third stage requires a more comprehensive approach in time. Thank you so much.

**CHN**, Representative
All protocols are observed. China aligns itself with the statement by Iraq on behalf of the G77 and China. This unity reform offered the UN an opportunity for self renewal by enhancing its governance capacity and better adapting to the evolving circumstances. We would like to offer five suggestions. First, we must remain true to the founding mission at a Time when multilateralism and the UN are under severe strain, it is more important than ever to recall the spirit that brought nations together 80 years ago. China believes that the reform must revitalize the UN authority and vitality, safeguard the purpose and principles of the UN Charter, enable the organization to keep pace with the times and ensure that it will continue to play a central role in international affairs and make greater contributions to the for the world peace and development. Second, we must strive for real results with high efficiency. China believes that the reform should focus on improving the quality and efficiency of the UN's work, as well as its agility, responsiveness and the resilience of this organization. In this process, wasteful spending, redundant formalities and excessive bureaucracy, more must be avoided. As Member States, we are all familiar with the burden of too many meetings and too many documents, and I believe there is a broader consensus on the need for change. The Working Group may start from this aspect to deliver visible improvements at early dates. Third, we must stay action oriented. This Working Group was established by the GA to improve the creation, delivery and review of the mandates by identifying principles and follow up actions. As essential as they are, principles alone cannot be enough. They must be matched with concrete, actionable measures. Only then can the reform be truly implemented with tangible results. Therefore, we believe that when discussing relevant principles, the Working Group should also design supporting implementation measures. This will ensure that the UN makes real steps and deliver real outcomes, thereby winning the future through real achievements. Fourth, we must strengthen research and analysis. The mandates of the Secretariat comes out of the nearly 4,000 resolutions and other resources. The sheer scale and complexity make it very difficult for Member States to see all the details. We believe that the Secretariat can do more. It should build on the Secretary General's reports and recommendations, summarize past lessons and put forward practical proposals for the Working Group. At the same time, the Co Chairs should heed the views of the broader UN membership to foster cooperation, build consensus and seek solidarity through consultation so that the work of this group can stand the test of history. Fifth, we must make a balanced approach to the three pillars. The GA resolution makes it very clear that the reform should ensure effective and efficient mandate delivery across all three pillars, namely peace and security, development and human rights of the United Nations. Let me conclude by reaffirming that China will continue to work together with all Member States and the Secretariat to improve the work of the UN and steer the global governance system toward a more justable and equitable direction. Thank you.

**IDN**, Representative
Thank you, Excellency. Let me join others to congratulate you and also the Permanent Representative of New Zealand on your assumption of duties as Co chairs of this informal adult working group. Second, we believe that open and inclusive approaches are fundamental to ensure broad participation from Member States, including in their national capacity or in the form of groupings. Third, we need to ensure that the process will align with other relevant parallel processes to avoid Duplication in particular this include the GA revitalization, ICOSOC reform, as well as the discussion on the reform of the Security Council. Excellency, we need outcomes that make a difference, not just more paper. In this regard, we also would like to ask a question to the how do the coaches envision the final product of this exercise? The information is crucial to help delegations calibrate their efforts and to contribute to the discussion so that we can focus on delivering tangible results. Excellencies, Distinguished Delegates, we share the Co Chair's view that the task is demanding, but it's not impossible. So let's continue keeping the process open, inclusive and focused to turn limited time into meaningful progress. Indonesia stands ready to contribute to that spirit. Thank you.

**THA**, Representative
Thank you. Kochai. Congratulations to both of you on this very important appointment and thank you so much for convening this meeting. Thailand alliance itself with statements delivered by Iraq on behalf of GS Vincent China and I wish to deliver this statement from our national capacity. Mandates are the property and responsibility of Member States. It is up to us to decide when mandates should be created, which mandates are still relevant and of course which mandates have become obsolete. The Secretary General has provide a thoughtful and data driven proposals. But of course the choices and the political will lie with us. This group has only six months to deliver recommendations. Given this short time frame, you must be pragmatic and focus on what is feasible and doable from the SDA report. One useful approach perhaps could be to identify a set of quick wins, practical measures that can be agreed upon early, such as streamlining reports and resolutions or piloting sunset clauses. These measures could be of course introduced on a trial basis before deciding on more ambitious reforms. Many of the six generous proposals, digital registry, self mandates, charter and clearance resolutions, streamlined reports and meetings, expiry clauses to avoid man that's continuing indefinitely and stronger accountability for results are all practical measures that could reduce duplications, free up resources and strengthen the UN's impact. But let us also be absolutely honest. Reform will not succeed if it is directed only at the Secretariat. We, the Member States, must also change our own working methods. We are the ones who adopt more and more resolutions, who request more reports, who create overlapping mandates and who too often instruct the UN to deliver within existing resources. These habits have made the UN larger, more complex and at times less efficient. The 80th anniversary of the UN is an important chance to strengthen multilateralism and show our taxpayers that this organization can adapt, deliver and remain relevant to the challenges of today and tomorrow. To conclude, it is our responsibility to make the UN stronger and adaptable with changing times. Thailand stand ready to work with our delegations so that we can hand over a more coherent, effective and trusted UN for generations to come. Thank you very much for your kind attention.

**MEX**, Representative
Mr. Ryder, distinguished CO Chairs from New Zealand and Jamaica, allow me to extend my congratulations on your appointment to lead the efforts of this working group. Mandates guide our collective action. Reviewing them with both prudence and boldness is an imperative. We cannot overlook. The magnitude of this challenge calls for vision and statesmanship. Mexico aspires for the mandate's review to be pragmatic, inclusive and grounded in consensus. A systemic approach is essential if we are to overcome fragmentation and strengthen the coherence of the organization's actions. Allow me to share a number of considerations that Mexico deems relevant for the process ahead, taking into consideration the three guiding questions provided this process must reinforce the UN's leadership across its three fundamental peace and security, development and human rights, while safeguarding the balance among them and consistently guided by the purposes of and principles enshrined in the Charter of the un. The mandates review should enhance coherence across the whole entire UN system, including mandates that go beyond the scope of the Secretariat for funds, programs, specialized agencies and other entities. It will be essential to promote dialogue within their respective governing bodies and to replicate this process across locations and levels of the system in order to prevent fragmentation and duplication. The review of mandates must be understood as a core element of a broader, comprehensive and ambitious reform, not as an isolated or gradual technical exercise. The goal is to transform the organization into a more effective, legitimate and results driven instrument. On the ground, the process must be guided by a clear and streamlined methodology underpinned by a forward looking vision that anticipates and avoids costly adjustments. It will be essential to design and implement targeted, systematic evaluation mechanisms that allow us to assess the relevance, validity and need of mandates, including, where appropriate, recommendations for determination in view of their fulfillment of solacence or redundancy. Adjustments to the periodicity of reviews, for instance, shifting from annual to biennial or triennial cycles, should also be considered to ensure a coherent, orderly and sustainable process over time. And the process must aim to deliver tangible, high impact results supported by efficient working methods, clear timelines and periodic evaluation mechanisms. The process must be guided by pragmatism, inclusiveness and openness, with transparency and legitimacy ensuring a collective sense of ownership and finally, an active role for the Secretariat. The Secretariat must play a proactive role by providing timely, relevant information and specialized technical support to the Working Group. This will be key to fostering a solid, well informed and effective deliberative process and to achieve concrete and implementable results. I thank you.

**IAHWG**, Co-Chair
I thank the distinguished representative of Mexico. I give the floor now to the distinguished representative of the United Kingdom, to be followed by Norway.

**GBR**, Representative
The UK welcomes the appointment of the CO Chairs for this ad hoc working group and thanks them for their efforts to date and in advance for the hard work that is to come. Given the short duration for this Working Group, we need to be focused on what we want to collectively achieve and in that regard, appreciate what Ambassador Wallace noted about the importance of an inclusive and transparent approach. To that I would add the value of evidence and so welcome the fact that there will be a discovery phase at the start of this process. From a UK perspective, we think it would be helpful for this Working Group to focus on the following three areas. First, we should develop a set of principles for the preparation of future mandates. The Secretary General set out a number of these in his report, such as the Secretariat providing more information in advance of any negotiation and increased budget transparency, both of which we would support in principle. The UK would also support shorter texts with fewer meetings and reports, commissioned and more comprehensive review clauses. And we welcome and appreciate USG Rider's update on these issues as well. Second, we should develop a common framework for how we will organize our work. We need to ensure we have clear parameters for how we review the implementation of the thousands of mandates we face as we go forward. With support from the Secretariat and using the new UN Mandate Source Registry, we should categorize mandates according to which of the UN's three pillars they support, their authorizing bodies and their funding modalities, and consider these factors in how we take our work forward. Third, it is essential that the Working Group makes tangible early progress on reviewing areas of duplication and unhelpful overlap. As a starting point, we we should request the Secretariat to provide information on the wealth of reports that are provided each year. This could be a meaningful data set for the Group to review and propose rationalization. We hope that within these six months we can both agree the principles to apply to future and previous mandates, as well as agree some concrete, tangible outcomes which will support the UN AT process. We look forward to the discussions and to working alongside the co facilitators and other Member States to advance this important strand of the UNHC process. Thank you.

My delegation aligns itself with a statement that was delivered on behalf of the G77 in China and the African Group and I will share the following perspectives in my national capacity in response to the guiding questions, Zimbabwe have used this ADWOC Working Group as a critical component of the UN80 initiative which should provide an open, transparent and inclusive platform for the mandate implementation review. The ADWERK Working Group is however working within a constrained timeframe and this calls for maximum collaboration, flexibility and ultimately consensus. The report by the Secretary General outlines three areas of mandates life cycle creation, delivery and review. My delegation wishes to propose that the work of the ADWERK Working Group should consequently follow a thematic approach based on these three areas. We further propose the compilation of a roadmap of activities of the Working Group. Central to this roadmap would be an elements paper prepared by the CO chairs based on the three focus areas and the Secretary General's recommendations. Member States could be invited to submit written inputs which would be synthesized into an Outcome document with a zero draft to be ready for circulation well ahead of the report back meeting on 15 December 2025. This approach would reduce the need for multiple physical meetings during the peak of Committee work, thereby easing the burden on smaller delegations. Further, we propose that the roadmap includes a provision for three interactive dialogue sessions between January and March 2026. These sessions could be utilized as consultative sessions with the objective of finalizing the outcome document. Additionally, Zimbabwe envisages the adoption of a resolution endorsing this outcome document before the conclusion of the 80th session. We welcome the commitment by the Secretariat to support Member states in implementing WE Extreme 2 and encourage the Secretary General to regularly update Member States on the progress in the activities outlined in the Report that are within its authority and we thank Mr. Guy Ryder for that reassurance. Let us therefore utilize this opportunity to work together towards a mandate in implementation review process which culminates in an agile fit for purpose United nations capable of effectively and efficiently responding to the world's pressing challenges. I wish to assure you coaches of Zimbabwe's constructive participation during deliberations. I thank you.
